<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>
Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are unaudited. It is the
opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of a normal recurring
nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, and management's discussion and analysis of financial condition and results of
operations, which appear in the Company's Annual Report to Shareholders and which are incorporated by reference into the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Certain
prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform with the current year's presentation, due primarily to the disclosure of more detailed information on the condensed consolidated statements
of earnings and the condensed consolidated statements of cash flows, as well as the transfer of Canadian Biscuits and Pet Snacks operations from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment to the
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;123,
"Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which did not result in compensation cost for stock options. The market value of restricted stock at date of grant is recorded as compensation expense over
the period of restriction. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock under its 2001 Performance Incentive Plan to eligible employees, giving them in
most instances all of the rights of shareholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber such shares and rights. Such shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if
certain employment conditions are not met. During the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted approximately 3.7&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S.&#151;based employees and
also issued to eligible non&#151;U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.6&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on the stock lapse in the first quarter of
2006. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the restricted shares and rights at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded compensation expense related to restricted
stock and other stock awards of $27&nbsp;million and $16&nbsp;million, respectively, for the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on
the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was $165&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company had stock-based employee compensation plans. The Company applies the recognition and measurement principles of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25,
"Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and related Interpretations in accounting for those plans. No compensation expense for employee stock options is reflected in net earnings as all options
granted under those plans had an exercise price equal to the market value of the common stock on the date of the grant. Net earnings, as reported, includes the after-tax impact of
compensation expense related to restricted stock. The following tables illustrate the effect on net earnings and earnings per share ("EPS") if the Company had applied the fair value recognition
provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;123 to stock-based employee compensation for the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Recently Adopted Accounting Standards:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted SFAS No.&nbsp;146, "Accounting for Costs Associated with Exit or Disposal Activities" for exit or disposal activities initiated after
December&nbsp;31, 2002. SFAS No.&nbsp;146 requires companies to recognize costs associated with exit or disposal activities when they are incurred rather than at the date of a commitment to an
exit or disposal plan. Costs covered by SFAS No.&nbsp;146 include lease termination costs and certain employee severance costs that are associated with a restructuring, discontinued operation, plant
closing or other exit or disposal activity. The adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;146 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows for
the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>11</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=2,SEQ=11,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=101600,FOLIO='11',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DK3898A.;15',USER='SLYUBOM',CD='11-AUG-2003;13:01' -->
<A NAME="page_dk3898_1_12"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Effective
January&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company adopted Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") Interpretation No.&nbsp;45, "Guarantor's Accounting and Disclosure Requirements for Guarantees,
Including Indirect Guarantees of Indebtedness of Others." Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 required the disclosure of certain guarantees existing at December&nbsp;31, 2002. In addition, Interpretation
No.&nbsp;45 required the recognition of a liability for the fair value of the obligation of qualifying guarantee activities that are initiated or modified after December&nbsp;31, 2002.
Accordingly, the Company has applied the recognition provisions of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 to guarantees initiated after December&nbsp;31, 2002. Adoption of Interpretation No.&nbsp;45 as of
January&nbsp;1, 2003 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial statements. See Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> for a further
discussion of guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued Interpretation No.&nbsp;46, "Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities." Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires a variable interest entity to be consolidated
by a company if that company is subject to a majority of the risk of loss from the variable interest entity's activities or is entitled to receive a majority of the entity's residual return or both.
Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 also provides criteria for determining whether an entity is a variable interest entity subject to consolidation. Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 requires immediate
consolidation of variable interest entities created after January&nbsp;31, 2003. For variable interest entities created prior to February&nbsp;1, 2003, consolidation is required on July&nbsp;1,
2003. The adoption of Interpretation No.&nbsp;46 did not have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
June&nbsp;30, 2003, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. owned approximately 84.1% of the Company's outstanding shares of capital stock. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s subsidiary, Altria Corporate
Services,&nbsp;Inc., provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary, corporate affairs,
information technology and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a management fee, were
$165&nbsp;million and $158&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, respectively, and $82&nbsp;million and $77&nbsp;million for the three months ended
June&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, respectively. </FONT></P>

payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates consisted of the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company repaid the remaining $1,150&nbsp;million to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. on the 7.0% note. At June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company had short-term
debt totaling $2,135&nbsp;million payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc., including amounts previously reclassified as long-term. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable
London Interbank Offered Rate. Included within the short-term debt is approximately $1,700&nbsp;million of notes due in the fourth quarter of 2003. The Company anticipates repaying these
notes on or before maturity using a combination of cash and the proceeds from the issuance of external debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Acquisitions and Divestitures:</U>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. The aggregate cost of acquisitions during the first six months of 2003 was $83&nbsp;million. During the first
quarter of 2002, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Australia for $62&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2002, the Company sold several small North American food businesses, most of which were previously classified as businesses held for sale. The net revenues and operating
results of the businesses held for sale, which were not significant, were excluded from the Company's condensed consolidated statements of earnings and no gain or loss was recognized on these sales.
The aggregate pre-tax proceeds received from sales of businesses during the first six months 2002 was $84&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company announced an agreement to sell its retail rice business in Germany, Austria and Denmark. This transaction has received approval from the German competition
authorities and is expected to close in the third quarter of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested were not material to the consolidated financial position or results of operations of the Company in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of damages are sought.
While the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's
consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture
activities, approximated $31&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2012, with $22&nbsp;million expiring through June&nbsp;30, 2004. The Company is required to
perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has recorded a liability of $21&nbsp;million at
June&nbsp;30, 2003 relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Non-amortizable
intangible assets consist substantially of brand names purchased through the Nabisco acquisition. Amortizable intangible assets consist primarily of certain trademark
licenses and non-compete agreements. Pre-tax amortization expense for intangible assets was $5&nbsp;million for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and
$3&nbsp;million for the three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. Based upon the amortizable intangible assets recorded in the condensed consolidated balance sheet at June&nbsp;30, 2003,
amortization expense for each of the next five years is estimated to be $10&nbsp;million or less. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
increase in goodwill and other intangible assets, net, during the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 of $456&nbsp;million is due primarily to currency translation ($398&nbsp;million) and
acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;8.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged retail food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
North America,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFNA") and Kraft Foods International,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFI"). Reportable segments for KFNA are organized and managed principally by product category. KFNA's segments are
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers; Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery; Beverages, Desserts and Cereals; and Oscar Mayer and Pizza. KFNA's food service business within the United States and its businesses in
Canada and Mexico are reported through the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment. KFI's operations are organized and managed by geographic location. KFI's segments are Europe, Middle East and Africa;
and Latin America and Asia Pacific. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of
segment profitability reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company transferred management responsibility of its Canadian Biscuits and Pet Snacks operations from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery segment to the
Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. Accordingly, all prior period amounts have been reclassified to reflect the transfer. </FONT></P>

consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=6,SEQ=18,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=418213,FOLIO='18',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DM3898A.;18',USER='FSTREET',CD='11-AUG-2003;19:07' -->
<A NAME="page_dm3898_1_19"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Recently Issued Accounting Pronouncements:</U>  </B></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;150, "Accounting for Certain Financial Instruments with Characteristics of both Liabilities and Equity." SFAS No.&nbsp;150 establishes standards
for classification and measurement of mandatorily redeemable financial instruments, obligations to repurchase the issuer's equity shares by transferring assets, and certain obligations to issue a
variable number of shares. SFAS No.&nbsp;150 is effective immediately for financial instruments entered into or modified after May&nbsp;31, 2003. SFAS No.&nbsp;150 is effective on July&nbsp;1,
2003 for financial instruments created or modified before May&nbsp;31, 2003. The adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;150 is not expected to have a material impact on the Company's 2003 consolidated
financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2003, the Emerging Issues Task Force ("EITF") reached a consensus on EITF Issue No.&nbsp;01-8, "Determining Whether an Arrangement Contains a Lease." EITF Issue
No.&nbsp;01-8 provides guidance on how to determine whether an arrangement contains a lease that is within the scope of SFAS No.&nbsp;13, "Accounting for Leases." EITF Issue
No.&nbsp;01-8 is effective for arrangements entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003. The Company does not expect the adoption of EITF Issue No.&nbsp;01-8 to
have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2003, the EITF reached a consensus on EITF Issue No.&nbsp;03-3, "Applicability of EITF Abstracts, Topic No.&nbsp;D-79, 'Accounting for Retroactive Insurance
Contracts Purchased by Entities Other Than Insurance Enterprises,' to Claims-Made Insurance Policies," regarding the accounting for claims-made insurance policies by the
insured party. EITF Issue No.&nbsp;03-3 provides guidance for determining whether a claims-made insurance policy contains a retroactive provision. EITF Issue
No.&nbsp;03-3 is effective for arrangements entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003. The Company does not expect the adoption of EITF Issue No.&nbsp;03-3 to
have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;149, "Amendment of Statement 133 on Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities." SFAS No.&nbsp;149 amends and clarifies financial accounting
and reporting for derivative instruments, including certain derivative instruments embedded in other contracts and for hedging activities under SFAS No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative
Instruments and Hedging Activities." In general, SFAS No.&nbsp;149 is effective for contracts entered into or modified after June&nbsp;30, 2003 and for hedging relationships designated after
June&nbsp;30, 2003. The Company does not expect the adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;149 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2002, the EITF issued EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21, "Revenue Arrangements with Multiple Deliverables," which addresses certain aspects of the accounting by a vendor for
arrangements under which it will perform multiple revenue-generating activities. Specifically, EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 addresses how to determine whether an arrangement involving
multiple deliverables contains more than one unit of accounting. EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 is effective for revenue arrangements entered into beginning July&nbsp;1, 2003. The Company
does not expect the adoption of EITF Issue No.&nbsp;00-21 to have a material impact on its 2003 consolidated financial statements. </FONT></P>

<TD WIDTH="12%"><FONT SIZE=2>Item 2.</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="72%" ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><B>MANAGEMENT'S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF</B></FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="12%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
</TR>
<TR VALIGN="TOP">
<TD WIDTH="12%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="72%" ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><B>FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS</B></FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="12%" ALIGN="RIGHT"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<!-- end of user-specified TAGGED TABLE -->


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States. At
June&nbsp;30, 2003, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 97.8% of the combined voting power of Kraft's outstanding capital stock and owned approximately 84.1% of the outstanding shares of Kraft's capital
stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company conducts its global business through two subsidiaries: Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFNA") and Kraft Foods International,&nbsp;Inc. ("KFI"). KFNA manages its operations by
product category, while KFI manages its operations by geographic region. KFNA's segments are Cheese, Meals and Enhancers; Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery; Beverages, Desserts and Cereals; and Oscar
Mayer and Pizza. KFNA's food service business within the United States and its businesses in Canada and Mexico are reported through the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment. KFI's segments are Europe,
Middle East and Africa; and Latin America and Asia Pacific. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is subject to a number of challenges that may adversely affect its businesses. These challenges, which are discussed below and under the "Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements,"
include: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>fluctuations
in commodity prices;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>movements
of foreign currencies against the U.S. dollar;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitive
challenges in various products and markets;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
trend toward increasing consolidation in the retail trade and consequent inventory reductions;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>changing
consumer preferences;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitors
with different profit objectives and less susceptibility to currency exchange rates; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>consumer
concerns about food safety, quality and health, including concerns about genetically modified organisms and obesity. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>To
confront these challenges, the Company continues to take steps to build the value of its brands, improve its food business portfolio with new product and marketing initiatives and to address
consumer concerns about food safety, quality and health. With obesity rates on the rise around the world, on July&nbsp;1, 2003, the Company announced a range of obesity related initiatives
addressing product nutrition, marketing practices, consumer information and public advocacy and dialogue. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, several factors contributed to lower than anticipated volume growth. These factors include trade inventory reductions, resulting from several customers experiencing
financial difficulty, warehouse consolidations, store closings and retailers' stated initiatives to reduce working capital, as well as the combined adverse effect of global economic weakness and
higher price gaps in some key categories and countries. To improve volume and share trends, the Company announced that it will increase marketing spending behind certain U.S. businesses in the balance
of 2003. The incremental investment is expected to be approximately $200&nbsp;million higher than previously planned amounts, with spending in the second half of 2003. The Company expects full year
diluted earnings per share in the range of $2.00-$2.05 for 2003. The Company also anticipates increased marketing spending behind certain U.S. businesses in 2004. Please refer to the Forward-Looking
and Cautionary Statements for a discussion of factors that could cause actual results and outcomes to differ materially from expected results. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
more fully discussed in the Debt and Liquidity section, during the first quarter of 2003, as a result of a judgment against Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s domestic tobacco subsidiary, the Company's
credit ratings were lowered, eliminating its access to the commercial paper market. Consequently, in April 2003, the Company began to borrow against its revolving credit facilities at an increased
borrowing cost. Subsequently, the Company regained access to the commercial paper market and began to reduce borrowings against its revolving credit facilities. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>20</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=20,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=831398,FOLIO='20',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898A.;29',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_21"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility, intensive price competition and influence consumer and trade buying patterns. KFNA's and KFI's businesses are subject to
fluctuating commodity costs, including dairy, coffee bean and cocoa costs. Dairy commodity prices on average have been lower than those incurred in 2002, while coffee and cocoa prices have been higher
than in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
December&nbsp;11, 2000, the Company acquired all of the outstanding shares of Nabisco Holdings Corp. ("Nabisco"). The closure of a number of Nabisco domestic and international facilities resulted
in severance and other exit costs of $379&nbsp;million, which were included in the adjustments for the allocation of the Nabisco purchase price. The closures will require total cash payments of
$373&nbsp;million, of which approximately $210&nbsp;million has been spent through June&nbsp;30, 2003. Substantially all closures are completed and the remaining payments relate to salary
continuation payments for severed employees and lease payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
integration of Nabisco into the operations of the Company has also resulted in the closure or reconfiguration of several of the Company's existing facilities. During the first quarter of 2002,
approximately 700 salaried employees elected to retire or terminate employment under voluntary retirement programs. As a result, the Company recorded a pre-tax charge of $142&nbsp;million during the
first quarter of 2002 related to these programs. In addition, during the first quarter of 2002, the Company recorded pre-tax integration related charges of $27&nbsp;million to consolidate production
lines in North America. During the second quarter of 2002, the Company recorded pre-tax integration related charges of $92&nbsp;million for the closing of a facility and other integration programs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2002, the Company sold several small North American food businesses, most of which were previously classified as businesses held for sale. The net revenues and operating
results of the businesses held for sale, which were not significant, were excluded from the Company's condensed consolidated statements of earnings and no gain or loss was recognized on these sales.
The aggregate pre-tax proceeds received from sales of businesses during the first six months of 2002 was $84&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. The aggregate cost of acquisitions during the first six months of 2003 was $83&nbsp;million. During the first
quarter of 2002, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Australia for $62&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
April&nbsp;2003, the Company announced an agreement to sell its retail rice business in Germany, Austria and Denmark. This transaction has received approval from the German competition
authorities and is expected to close in the third quarter of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested were not material to the consolidated financial position or results of operations of the Company in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>21</FONT></P>

following events occurred during the first six months and second quarter of 2002 that affected the comparability of statement of earnings amounts: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note&nbsp;8. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, management reviews operating companies income, which is defined as operating income
before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help
investors analyze business performances and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Six Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 2003  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first six months of 2003 increased 0.9% over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts and Cereals segment, contributions from new
products and growth in developing markets, partially offset by the impact of divested businesses, a reduction in trade inventories and the combined adverse effect of global economic weakness and
higher price gaps in certain categories and countries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the first six months of 2003 increased $540&nbsp;million (3.7%) over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to favorable currency ($228 million), higher pricing
($213&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity and currency devaluation-driven costs) and higher volume/mix ($128&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of businesses divested in 2002
($49&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income for the first six months of 2003 increased $193&nbsp;million (6.6%) over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation programs
($142&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($119&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of cost increases ($38&nbsp;million, including productivity and synergy savings), and favorable currency
($24&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($60&nbsp;million)
and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). The higher benefit costs were primarily related to pension and stock compensation costs. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements have increased net revenues by $228&nbsp;million and operating income by $24&nbsp;million over the first six months of 2002. These increases in net revenues and operating income
are due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and other currencies, partially offset by the strength of the U.S. dollar against certain Latin American currencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $108&nbsp;million from the first six months of 2002. This decrease is due to the Company's refinancing of notes payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.,
lower short-term interest rates and the use of free cash flow to pay down debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $1,797&nbsp;million for the first six months of 2003 increased $203 million (12.7%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to growth in operating income and lower interest
expense. Diluted and basic earnings per share ("EPS"), which were both $1.04 for the first six months of 2003, increased by 13.0% over 2002. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>24</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=24,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=561752,FOLIO='24',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898A.;29',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_25"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Three Months Ended June&nbsp;30, 2003  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the second quarter of 2003 increased 1.7% over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts and Cereals segment, contributions from new
products, the shift in shipments supporting the Easter holiday, which fell into the second quarter of 2003 versus the first quarter of 2002, and growth in developing markets. These gains were
partially offset by the impact of divested businesses, trade inventory reductions and the combined adverse effect of global economic weakness and higher price gaps in certain categories and countries. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the second quarter of 2003 increased $328&nbsp;million (4.4%) over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to favorable currency ($147&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix
($100&nbsp;million) and higher pricing ($97&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity and currency devaluation-driven costs, partially offset by higher promotional spending and product returns
from new biscuit product launches that fell short of expectations). These increases were partially offset by the impact of 2002 divested businesses ($27&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income for the second quarter of 2003 increased $9&nbsp;million (0.6%) over the comparable 2002 period, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for integration costs
($92&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($30&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($18&nbsp;million), partially offset by cost increases, net of higher pricing ($66&nbsp;million, due primarily
to higher commodity costs, increased promotional spending and product returns from new biscuit product launches that fell short of expectations), and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher
benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements have increased net revenues by $147&nbsp;million and operating income by $18&nbsp;million over the second quarter of 2002. These increases in net revenues and operating income
are due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and other currencies, partially offset by the strength of the U.S. dollar against certain Latin American currencies. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $57&nbsp;million from the second quarter of 2002. This decrease is due to the Company's refinancing of notes payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.,
lower short-term interest rates and the use of free cash flow to pay down debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $949&nbsp;million for the second quarter of 2003 increased $48 million (5.3%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to lower interest expense and growth in operating
income. Diluted and basic EPS, which were both $0.55 for the second quarter of 2003, increased by 5.8% over 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company transferred management responsibility of its Canadian Biscuits and Pet Snacks operations from the Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery
segment to the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, which contains the Company's other Canadian businesses. Accordingly, all prior period amounts have been reclassified to reflect the transfer. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first six months of 2003 increased 1.9% over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts and Cereals segment and contributions from
new products, partially offset by the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002, a reduction in trade inventories and consumption weakness in certain categories. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $162&nbsp;million (1.5%) over the first six months of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($118&nbsp;million), higher pricing
($42&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($12&nbsp;million), partially offset by the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 increased $213 million (8.6%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation programs
($135&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($102&nbsp;million), and higher pricing, net of cost increases ($22&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher fixed overhead costs (including higher
benefit costs). As discussed above in the Business Environment section, the Company announced that it will increase planned marketing spending by approximately $200&nbsp;million behind certain U.S.
businesses in the second half of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of KFNA's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Cheese, Meals and Enhancers.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the first six months of 2003 increased 1.2% over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to
higher shipments in Canada, food service and Mexico, partially offset by lower consumption and reduced trade inventories in certain cheese and enhancers businesses. Volume in Canada and Mexico
increased, driven by new product introductions. Volume in the food service business in the United States also increased due to higher shipments of cheese and meat to national accounts and increased
demand for ingredient products. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $17&nbsp;million (0.4%) over the first six months of 2002, due to favorable currency ($12&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix
($5&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=7,SEQ=26,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=1008918,FOLIO='26',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898A.;29',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 increased $69 million (6.3%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation programs
($60&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($35&nbsp;million), and favorable costs ($23&nbsp;million, including favorable commodity costs and productivity savings), partially offset by unfavorable
volume/mix ($27&nbsp;million) and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the first six months of 2003 decreased 4.0% from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily
to consumption weakness in cookies, reduced trade inventories and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $24&nbsp;million (1.0%) over the first six months of 2002, due primarily to higher volume/mix ($36 million), partially offset by the
divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002 ($10&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 decreased $8 million (1.7%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to unfavorable costs ($5&nbsp;million, including higher
commodity costs) and higher fixed overhead costs, partially offset by lower marketing, administration and research costs ($39&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Beverages, Desserts and Cereals.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the first six months of 2003 increased 6.9% over the comparable period in 2002, due primarily to
higher shipments of ready-to-drink beverages, which were aided by new product introductions. Volume declined in coffee, due primarily to reduced consumption, as higher prices resulted in category and
share declines. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $84&nbsp;million (3.6%) over the first six months of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($54&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($30&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 increased $132 million (22.0%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for integration costs
($59&nbsp;million) and separation programs ($47&nbsp;million), lower marketing, administration and research costs ($35&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($19&nbsp;million), partially offset
by higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Oscar Mayer and Pizza.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the first six months of 2003 increased slightly over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to
volume gains in frozen pizza, bacon and soy-based meat alternatives, offset by lower consumption of cold cuts. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $37&nbsp;million (2.4%) over the first six months of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($23&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($14&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 increased $20&nbsp;million (6.8%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charges for separation programs
($25&nbsp;million) and integration costs ($7&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of cost increases ($9&nbsp;million), and higher volume/mix ($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher
marketing, administration and research costs ($15&nbsp;million) and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the first six months of 2003 decreased 2.0% from the first six months of 2002, due to the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002, partially
offset by growth in developing markets, new product introductions and the acquisitions of a snacks business in Turkey and a biscuits business in Egypt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues increased $378&nbsp;million (10.0%) over the first six months of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency ($216&nbsp;million), higher pricing
($171&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity and currency devaluation-driven costs in Latin America) and the impact of acquisitions ($20&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of
divestitures ($39&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 decreased $18&nbsp;million (3.3%) from the first six months of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs
($70&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures ($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable currency ($23&nbsp;million), the 2002 pre-tax charges for integration costs
($17&nbsp;million) and separation programs ($7&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of cost increases ($16&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of KFI's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East and Africa.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume for the first six months of 2003 increased 1.4% over the comparable period of 2002, driven by volume
growth across the Central and Eastern Europe, Middle East and Africa region, new product introductions and the recent acquisition of a biscuits business in Egypt as well as a snacks business
acquisition in Turkey during the third quarter of 2002, partially offset by the volume impact of price competition and consumer down-trading to lower-priced alternatives in select markets. Snacks
volume increased, benefiting from the recent acquisition of a biscuits business in Egypt and the 2002 acquisition in Turkey, and the continued growth of confectionery businesses in Russia and Poland,
partially offset by lower volume in select markets due to price competition. Beverages volume also increased, due primarily to increased coffee shipments in many markets, including Germany, Poland,
Romania and Russia. In convenient meals, volume increased due to higher shipments of canned meats in Italy, partially offset by declines in Germany. Cheese volume declined, due primarily to the impact
of price competition in Germany and Spain and lower shipments in the Middle East, partially offset by gains in cream cheese and cheese slices in Italy. Grocery volume was comparable with the prior
year. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=9,SEQ=28,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=688008,FOLIO='28',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898B.;7',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_29"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the first six months of 2003 increased $473&nbsp;million (17.1%) over the comparable period of 2002, due to favorable currency ($442&nbsp;million), the impact of acquisitions
($20&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($17&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower pricing ($6&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 increased $41&nbsp;million (10.6%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency ($51&nbsp;million) and the
2002 pre-tax charge for separation programs ($5&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower pricing and cost increases ($22&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America and Asia Pacific.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume for the first six months of 2003 decreased 6.7% from the comparable period in 2002, due to the
divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002, political and economic
instability in Venezuela during the first quarter of 2003 and economic weakness in Argentina, partially offset by growth in most Asia Pacific markets. Snacks volume decreased, due primarily to
political and economic instability in Venezuela, confectionery market decline in Brazil and a decline in Argentina, partially offset by biscuits volume growth in many markets, including Brazil,
Colombia, Central America, Australia, Southeast Asia and China. In grocery, volume declined in Latin America, due primarily to the sale of a bakery ingredients business in the fourth quarter of 2002.
In beverages, volume grew in both coffee and refreshment beverages. Coffee volume increased due primarily to higher shipments to China. Refreshment beverages volume increased, due to growth in most
markets, including Brazil, Venezuela and the Philippines, aided by new product introductions. In cheese, volume increased due to higher shipments in Japan, partially offset by declines in Indonesia
and political and economic instability in Venezuela. Convenient meals volume also grew, benefiting from gains in Argentina. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net revenues decreased $95&nbsp;million (9.2%) from the first six months of 2002, due to unfavorable currency ($226&nbsp;million), the divestiture of a Latin
American bakery ingredients business in 2002 ($39&nbsp;million) and lower volume/mix ($7&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($177&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity and
currency devaluation-driven costs). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the first six months of 2003 decreased $59&nbsp;million (36.0%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research
costs ($73&nbsp;million), unfavorable currency ($28&nbsp;million), lower volume/mix ($6&nbsp;million) and the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002
($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing, net of cost increases ($38&nbsp;million), and the 2002 pre-tax charges for integration costs ($17&nbsp;million) and separation programs
($2&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc.</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Operating Results  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the second quarter of 2003 increased 2.5% over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to increased shipments in the Beverages, Desserts and Cereals segment,
contributions from new products and the shift in shipments supporting the Easter holiday, which fell into the second quarter of 2003 versus the first quarter of 2002, partially offset by trade
inventory reductions, lower consumption in certain categories and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $76&nbsp;million (1.4%) over the second quarter of 2002, due primarily to higher volume/mix ($65 million), favorable currency
($18&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, partially offset by higher trade spending to manage price gaps, primarily on certain cheese categories, returns of new biscuit products that did not perform as
expected and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 increased $14&nbsp;million (1.0%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charge for integration costs
($75&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($14&nbsp;million), partially offset by cost increases, net of higher pricing (aggregating $65&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs, increased
promotional spending in certain categories and returns of new biscuit products that did not perform as expected), and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). As discussed above
in the Business Environment section, the Company announced that it will increase planned marketing spending by approximately $200&nbsp;million behind certain U.S. businesses in the second half of
2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of KFNA's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Cheese, Meals and Enhancers.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the second quarter of 2003 increased 2.7% over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the
shift in Easter shipments and volume gains in Mexico, Canada and food service. In cheese, volume increased due to the Easter timing shift; however, cheese shares declined in a number of categories,
driven by higher price gaps versus competitors. In Mexico and Canada, volume increased, aided by new product introductions. Volume in the food service business in the United States also increased, due
to higher shipments to national accounts and increased demand for ingredient products. In enhancers, volume declined due to reduced consumption and trade inventory reductions, primarily in spoonable
salad dressings and barbecue sauce. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>30</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=11,SEQ=30,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=144864,FOLIO='30',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898B.;7',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_31"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $46&nbsp;million (1.9%) over the second quarter of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($40&nbsp;million) and favorable currency
($18&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower pricing ($12 million, primarily higher trade spending in response to lower dairy costs). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 decreased $17&nbsp;million (2.7%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to lower pricing and unfavorable costs
($27&nbsp;million) and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs), partially offset by lower marketing, administration and research costs ($14&nbsp;million), the 2002 pre-tax
charge for integration costs ($8 million) and higher volume/mix ($8&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Biscuits, Snacks and Confectionery.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the second quarter of 2003 decreased 6.0% from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily
to lower shipments in biscuits and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002. In biscuits, volume declined due to reduced consumption in cookies reflecting both category declines and
lower response from promotional programs. In snacks, volume increased driven by marketing programs and contributions from new products. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues decreased $23&nbsp;million (1.9%) from the second quarter of 2002, due to product returns associated with new biscuit products ($17&nbsp;million),
lower volume/mix ($6&nbsp;million) and the divestiture of a small confectionery business in 2002 ($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 decreased $28&nbsp;million (10.0%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to cost increases, net of higher pricing (aggregating
$32&nbsp;million, driven by higher commodity costs and product returns associated with new biscuit products), and higher fixed overhead costs, partially offset by lower marketing, administration and
research costs ($41&nbsp;million, including synergy savings). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Beverages, Desserts and Cereals.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the second quarter of 2003 increased 8.6% over the comparable period in 2002, due primarily to
higher shipments of ready-to-drink beverages, which were aided by new product introductions. Volume also increased in dry packaged desserts and frozen toppings due primarily to the shift in Easter
shipments. Coffee volume declined due to lower consumption, as higher prices resulted in category and share declines. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $50&nbsp;million (4.3%) over the second quarter of 2002, due to higher volume/mix ($35&nbsp;million) and higher pricing
($15&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 increased $65&nbsp;million (22.3%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to the 2002 pre-tax charge for integration costs
($59&nbsp;million), lower marketing, administration and research costs ($17&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($16&nbsp;million), partially offset by unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing
($10&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs), and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Oscar Mayer and Pizza.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume in the second quarter of 2003 decreased 1.2% from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to lower
volume in cold cuts and hot dogs, partially offset by contributions from new products in lunch combinations and pizza. Volume declined in cold cuts and hot dogs due to increased price gaps versus
regional price-oriented brands. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter 2003, net revenues increased $3&nbsp;million (0.4%) over the second quarter of 2002, due to higher pricing ($7&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending to
narrow price gaps), partially offset by lower volume/mix ($4&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 decreased $6&nbsp;million (3.8%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to lower volume/mix ($5&nbsp;million), higher
marketing, administration and research costs ($5&nbsp;million) and higher fixed overhead costs (including higher benefit costs), partially offset by the 2002 </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>31</FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_do3898_1_32"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>pre-tax
charge for integration costs ($7&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of cost increases ($4&nbsp;million, including favorable cheese costs in pizza and increased promotional spending to
narrow price gaps). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
for the second quarter of 2003 decreased 0.9% from the second quarter of 2002, due to the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002, the impact of
intense price competition and consumer down-trading to lower-priced alternatives, partially offset by the shift in Easter shipments, new product introductions, growth in developing markets and the
acquisitions of a snacks business in Turkey and a biscuits business in Egypt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues increased $252&nbsp;million (13.0%) over the second quarter of 2002, due to favorable currency ($129&nbsp;million), higher pricing
($98&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity and currency devaluation-driven cost increases in Latin America), higher volume/mix ($35&nbsp;million) and the acquisitions of a snacks business in
Turkey and a biscuits business in Egypt ($11&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($21&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 decreased $3&nbsp;million (1.0%) from the second quarter of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs
($45&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), the impact of divestitures ($4&nbsp;million) and devaluation-driven costs in Latin America, partially offset by the 2002 pre-tax charge for
integration costs ($17&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($16&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($16&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of KFI's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East and Africa.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume for the second quarter of 2003 increased 1.6% over the comparable period of 2002, driven by volume
growth across the Central and Eastern Europe, Middle East and Africa region, benefiting from acquisitions and higher volume in Poland, Russia and Romania, partially offset by price competition in
select markets impacting the European Union region. Snacks volume increased, benefiting from acquisitions, the shift in Easter shipments, the continued growth of the confectionery business in Russia,
partially offset by volume declines in France, Bulgaria and the Ukraine due to the impact of recent price increases. Beverages volume also increased in both coffee and refreshment beverages, as higher
shipments of </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>32</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=13,SEQ=32,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=358998,FOLIO='32',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898B.;7',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_33"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>coffee
in most markets, particularly Russia and Poland, and higher shipments of refreshment beverages were partially offset by a decline in coffee in France and the United Kingdom due to increased
price competition. In convenient meals, volume increased, due primarily to higher shipments of canned meats in Italy. Grocery volume increased, benefiting from growth in Germany, Spain and Egypt,
partially offset by lower results in Italy and the United Kingdom. Cheese volume declined, impacted by price competition in Germany and Spain and lower shipments in the Middle East, partially offset
by gains in cream cheese in the United Kingdom and the Nordic region, benefiting from increased marketing and new product introductions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues for the second quarter of 2003 increased $264&nbsp;million (18.6%) over the comparable period of 2002, due to favorable currency ($237&nbsp;million), the acquisitions of a snacks
business in Turkey and a biscuits business in Egypt ($11&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($11&nbsp;million) and higher pricing ($5&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 increased $20&nbsp;million (9.4%) over the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to favorable currency ($30&nbsp;million), partially
offset by higher marketing, administration and research costs ($6&nbsp;million) and unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($6&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America and Asia Pacific.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Volume for the second quarter of 2003 decreased 4.5% from the comparable period in 2002, due to the
divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002, partially offset by growth in several Asia Pacific markets and the shift in Easter shipments. Snacks volume increased, due
primarily to the shift in Easter shipments and growth in Asia Pacific, partially offset by a decline in Argentina. In beverages, volume growth in Brazil, Venezuela, China and the Philippines was
partially offset by a decline in Argentina. Convenient meals volume grew, due primarily to increased shipments in Argentina. In grocery, volume declined in Latin America due to the divestiture of a
bakery ingredients business. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the second quarter of 2003, net revenues decreased $12&nbsp;million (2.3%) from the second quarter of 2002, due to unfavorable currency ($108&nbsp;million) and the divestiture of a Latin
American bakery ingredients business in 2002 ($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($93&nbsp;million, reflecting higher currency devaluation-driven costs) and higher volume/mix
($24&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income for the second quarter of 2003 decreased $23&nbsp;million (26.4%) from the comparable period of 2002, due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs
($39&nbsp;million), unfavorable currency ($14&nbsp;million) and the divestiture of a Latin American bakery ingredients business in 2002 ($4&nbsp;million), partially offset by the 2002 pre-tax
charge for integration costs ($17&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($15&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of cost increases ($5&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Financial Review</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by Operating Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net cash provided by operating activities was $1.6&nbsp;billion compared with $1.1&nbsp;billion in the comparable 2002 period. The increase in net cash
provided by operating activities is due primarily to a lower use of cash to satisfy amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc., and a lower level of cash used to fund working capital. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Used in Investing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>One
element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly investigating
potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses that are outside its core categories or that do not meet its growth or profitability targets. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>33</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<!-- ZEQ.=14,SEQ=33,EFW="2116254",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=1016561,FOLIO='33',FILE='DISK027:[03CHI8.03CHI3898]DO3898B.;7',USER='MBLOUNT',CD='12-AUG-2003;14:17' -->
<A NAME="page_do3898_1_34"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net cash used in investing activities was $561&nbsp;million, compared with $405&nbsp;million in the first six months of 2002. This increase primarily reflects
the cash received from the 2002 divestiture of several North American food businesses, an increase in capital expenditures and an increase in cash used for acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Net
Cash Provided by (Used in) Financing Activities</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first six months of 2003, net cash provided by financing activities was $268&nbsp;million, compared with net cash used in financing activities of $763&nbsp;million during the first six
months of 2002. The difference is due primarily to higher debt in 2003 (including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates), compared with the repayment of debt in 2002 (including
amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Debt
and Liquidity</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Debt.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company's total debt, including amounts due to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates, was $15.5&nbsp;billion at
June&nbsp;30, 2003 and $14.4&nbsp;billion at December&nbsp;31, 2002. The increase in total debt reflects temporary borrowings made on existing revolving credit facilities after access to the
commercial paper market was eliminated for the Company. The Company has subsequently regained access to the commercial paper markets. An increased level of cash and cash equivalents has resulted from
these borrowings. This cash, which was $1.5&nbsp;billion at June&nbsp;30, 2003 (up from $215&nbsp;million at December&nbsp;31, 2002), will be used to meet ongoing working capital requirements
as well as debt maturities. The Company's debt-to-equity ratio was 0.56 at June&nbsp;30, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company repaid the remaining $1,150 million of the 7.0% long-term notes payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. and affiliates. At June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company
had short-term debt totaling $2,135 million payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc., including amounts previously reclassified as long-term. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London
Interbank Offered Rate. Included within the short-term debt is approximately $1,700&nbsp;million of notes due in the fourth quarter of 2003. The Company anticipates repaying these notes on or before
maturity using a combination of cash and the proceeds from the issuance of external debt. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Credit Ratings.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Following a $10.1&nbsp;billion judgment on March&nbsp;21, 2003 against Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s domestic tobacco
subsidiary, Philip Morris USA Inc., the three major credit rating agencies took a series of ratings actions resulting in the lowering of the Company's short-term and long-term debt ratings, despite
the fact the Company is not a party to, nor has exposure to this litigation. Moody's lowered the Company's short-term debt rating from "P-1" to
"P-2" and its long-term debt rating from "A2" to "A3", with negative outlook. Standard&nbsp;&amp; Poor's lowered the Company's short-term debt rating from "A-1" to "A-2" and its long-term debt rating
from "A-" to "BBB+", with stable outlook. Fitch Rating Services lowered the Company's short-term debt rating from "F-1" to "F-2" and its long-term debt rating from "A" to "BBB", with stable outlook.
As a result of the credit rating agencies' actions, borrowing costs for the Company increased. None of the Company's debt agreements requires accelerated repayment in the event of a decrease in credit
ratings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Credit Lines.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company maintains revolving credit facilities that have historically been used to support the issuance of commercial
paper. However, as a result of the credit rating agencies' actions, the Company's access to the commercial paper market was eliminated. As a consequence, in April&nbsp;2003, the Company began to
borrow against existing credit facilities to repay maturing commercial paper and to fund normal working capital needs. By the end of May, the Company regained its access to the commercial paper
markets. At June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company's credit facilities included a $2.0&nbsp;billion, multi-year revolving credit facility expiring in July&nbsp;2006 and a $3.0&nbsp;billion, 364-day
revolving credit facility expiring in July&nbsp;2003. In July&nbsp;2003, the Company's existing $3.0&nbsp;billion, 364-day revolving credit facility was terminated and was replaced by a new
$2.5&nbsp;billion, 364-day revolving credit facility that expires in July&nbsp;2004. At June&nbsp;30, 2003 and at August&nbsp;8, 2003, credit lines for the Company and the related activity
were as follows (in&nbsp;billions of dollars): </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's revolving credit facilities, which are for the sole use of the Company, require the maintenance of a minimum net worth of $18.2&nbsp;billion. The Company met this
covenant at June&nbsp;30, 2003 and expects to continue to meet this covenant. The foregoing revolving credit facilities do not include any other financial tests, any credit rating triggers or any
provisions that could require the posting of collateral. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to the above, certain international subsidiaries of the Company maintain uncommitted credit lines to meet the short-term working capital needs of the international businesses. These credit
lines, which amounted to approximately $0.6&nbsp;billion as of June&nbsp;30, 2003, are for the sole use of the Company's international businesses. At June&nbsp;30, 2003, borrowings on these
lines amounted to approximately $0.2&nbsp;billion. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Guarantees.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>As discussed in Note&nbsp;6. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Contingencies,</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> the Company had third-party
guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition and divestiture activities, of approximately $31&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2003. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through
2012, with $22&nbsp;million expiring through June 30, 2004. The Company is required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve
performance measures. The Company has recorded a liability of $21&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2003 relating to these guarantees. In addition, at June&nbsp;30, 2003, the Company was
contingently liable for $117&nbsp;million of guarantees related to its own performance. These include surety bonds related to dairy commodity purchases and guarantees related to letters of credit
and taxes. Guarantees do not have, and are not expected to have, a significant impact on the Company's liquidity. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company believes that its cash from operations and existing credit facilities will provide sufficient liquidity to meet its working capital needs, planned capital expenditures and payment of its
anticipated quarterly dividends. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><U>Equity
and Dividends</U> </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company repurchased 2.8&nbsp;million shares of its Class&nbsp;A common stock during the first six months of 2003 at a cost of $86&nbsp;million. At June&nbsp;30, 2003, cumulative
repurchases under its previously announced $500&nbsp;million authority totaled 7.2&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A common stock at an aggregate cost of $256&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock under its 2001 Performance Incentive Plan to eligible employees, giving them in
most instances all of the rights of stockholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber such shares and rights. These shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if
certain employment conditions are not met. During the first
quarter of 2003, the Company granted approximately 3.7&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S.-based employees and also issued to eligible non-U.S. employees rights to receive
approximately 1.6&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on the stock lapse in the first quarter of 2006. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the restricted shares and rights at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded compensation expense related to restricted
stock and other stock </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>35</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>awards
of $27&nbsp;million and $16&nbsp;million, respectively, for the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed
consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was $165&nbsp;million at June&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Dividends
paid in the first six months of 2003 and 2002 were $520&nbsp;million and $451&nbsp;million, respectively, an increase of 15.3%, reflecting a higher dividend rate in 2003, partially
offset by a lower number of shares outstanding as a result of share repurchases. The present annualized dividend rate is $0.60 per common share. The declaration of dividends is subject to the
discretion of the Company's Board of Directors and will depend on various factors, including the Company's net earnings, financial condition, cash requirements, future prospects and other factors
deemed relevant by the Company's Board of Directors. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Market Risk</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company operates globally, with manufacturing and sales facilities in numerous locations around the world, and utilizes certain financial instruments to manage its foreign currency and commodity
exposures, which primarily relate to forecasted transactions. Derivative financial instruments are used by the Company, principally to reduce exposures to market risks resulting from fluctuations in
foreign exchange rates and commodity prices by creating offsetting exposures. The Company is not a party to leveraged derivatives and, by policy, does not use financial instruments for speculative
purposes. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Substantially
all of the Company's derivative financial instruments are effective as hedges under Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;133, "Accounting for Derivative
Instruments and Hedging Activities." During the six months and three months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and 2002, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. At June&nbsp;30, 2003,
the Company was hedging forecasted transactions for periods not exceeding seventeen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) to be
reclassified to the consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Foreign exchange rates.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company uses forward foreign exchange contracts and foreign currency options to mitigate its exposure to
changes in foreign currency exchange rates from third-party and intercompany forecasted transactions. The primary currencies to which the Company is exposed, based on the size and location of its
operations, include the euro, British pound and Canadian dollar. At June&nbsp;30, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002, the Company had option and forward foreign exchange contracts with aggregate
notional amounts of $1.1&nbsp;billion and $575&nbsp;million, respectively, which are comprised of contracts for the purchase and sale of foreign currencies. The effective portion of unrealized
gains and losses associated with forward contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) until the underlying hedged transactions are reported on the
Company's consolidated statement of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Commodities.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>The Company is exposed to price risk related to forecasted purchases of certain commodities used as raw materials by the
Company's businesses. Accordingly, the Company uses commodity forward contracts, as cash flow hedges, primarily for coffee, cocoa, milk and cheese. Commodity futures and options are also used to hedge
the price of certain commodities, including milk, coffee, cocoa, wheat, corn, sugar and soybean oil. In general, commodity forward contracts qualify for the normal purchase exception under SFAS
No.&nbsp;133 and are, therefore, not subject to the provisions of SFAS No.&nbsp;133. At June&nbsp;30, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002, the Company had net long commodity positions of
$497&nbsp;million and $544&nbsp;million, respectively. Unrealized gains or losses on net commodity positions were immaterial at June&nbsp;30, 2003 and December&nbsp;31, 2002. The effective
portion of unrealized gains and losses on commodity futures and option contracts is deferred as a component of accumulated other comprehensive earnings (losses) and is recognized as a component of
cost of sales in the Company's consolidated statement of earnings when the related inventory is sold. </FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE ALIGN="CENTER" WIDTH="120">
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>36</FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Use

results of operations for the three and six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and June&nbsp;30, 2002, or the Company's cash flows for the six months ended June&nbsp;30, 2003 and June&nbsp;30,
2002. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>See
